mr-sm flex items-center">Bio<svg class="fill-inherit ml-xxs" height="16" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><title>Bio</title><path d="M12.207 5.207L6.26 11.154 4.846 9.74l5.947-5.947L9 2h5v5l-1.793-1.793zM7 2v1H3v10h10V9h1v4a1 1 0 0 1-1 1H3a1 1 0 0 1-1-1V3a1 1 0 0 1 1-1h4z" fill-rule="nonzero"></path></svg></span></a><a class="twitter-link" href="https://twitter.com/@mffisher"><span class="pointer gray-darkest fill-gray-darkest hover-blue hover-fill-blue flex items-center">Follow<svg class="fill-inherit ml-xxs" height="16" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><title>Follow</title><path d="M5.403 13.671c5.283 0 8.172-4.413 8.172-8.241 0-.125 0-.25-.008-.374A5.872 5.872 0 0 0 15 3.556a5.695 5.695 0 0 1-1.65.456 2.902 2.902 0 0 0 1.263-1.602 5.727 5.727 0 0 1-1.824.703 2.858 2.858 0 0 0-4.064-.126 2.915 2.915 0 0 0-.83 2.768 8.132 8.132 0 0 1-5.92-3.027 2.913 2.913 0 0 0 .889 3.867 2.833 2.833 0 0 1-1.304-.363v.037c0 1.379.964 2.566 2.304 2.84a2.844 2.844 0 0 1-1.297.05 2.879 2.879 0 0 0 2.684 2.01A5.733 5.733 0 0 1 1 12.37a8.082 8.082 0 0 0 4.403 1.3" fill-rule="evenodd"></path></svg></span></a></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="mb-md gray-dark font--subhead font-xxs" data-qa="timestamp"><div class="display-date">September 27, 2019 at 12:11 PM EDT</div></div><div class="article-body"><div class="teaser-content"><section><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">They dont ordinarily agree with each other. They watch different channels, hear different versions of the news and view neighbors across a gaping, painful political<b> </b>divide. But in swing districts across the country, the idea of impeaching the president has brought some Americans together: Theyre wary of deploying the Constitutions ultimate weapon  one that takes the decision about who is president out of voters hands.</p></div></section></div><div class="remainder-content"><section><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Derek Tsao is a Republican in California who has grown tired of President Trumps behavior. Curtis Johnson is a Democrat in Florida who could never quite fathom why his fellow Americans chose a man like Trump. Lisa Foulds is a lifelong Republican in suburban Virginia whose kids have pushed her toward the center, so much so that she voted for a Democrat for Congress last year.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">They all say the president may have crossed a line when he pressed his Ukrainian counterpart to investigate one of Trumps main political rivals. And despite their political differences, they say the Democrats move this week to start impeachment proceedings against Trump is the wrong tactic at the wrong time.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><figure class="pad-top-xs mb-md ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns center hide-for-print"><div class="powa-wrapper"><div class="powa-skip" data-ad-bar="1" data-aspect-ratio="0.5625" data-blurb="true" data-org="wapo" data-playthrough="true" data-uuid="7cb6849e-5c02-4dab-b333-69db571725e7"></div></div></figure></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Polls have shown that public opinion has shifted slightly in favor of impeachment, but many still see it as an exercise in futility, as Johnson put it.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The retired steelworker from Indiana, now living in New Smyrna Beach, Fla., said hes eager for Democrats to find a candidate who can beat Trump next year, but he fears that impeaching the president will make Trumps reelection more likely. Theres not enough time before the election and nothing will come of it, said Johnson, 71. This is going to hurt the Democrats because everyones going to say, Youre putting all your energy into<span> this</span>?</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Tsao, 27, who is studying to be a physical therapist, has followed this weeks news only glancingly, but hes all for investigating any credible accusations.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_2"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">If a crime has been alleged, you should find out more about it, he said. I fear, though, that its just another anti-Trump move.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_2"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Launching an investigation and potentially putting Trump on trial in the Senate strikes Foulds, a 50-year-old who still considers herself a Republican after voting for independent Gary Johnson in 2016, as a waste of the taxpayers money.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">For something as trivial as gaining dirt on somebody? It just seems petty, she said. I just think it has to be much more egregious.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">As events in Washington unfolded at a breakneck pace this week, many Democrats and Republicans interviewed in swing districts across seven states were united in their exhaustion  with politics, with polarization and, even among some of his supporters, with the president. Many said they chose not to follow every twist and turn in the Ukraine story because their views about Trump had long ago solidified, pro or con.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_3"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Voters across the partisan spectrum argued that next years election  not impeachment  is the best way to resolve the countrys struggle with a divisive, unpopular president who now stands accused of betraying the nations interests.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_3"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><figure class="pad-top-xs mb-md ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns center hide-for-print"><div class="powa-wrapper"><div class="powa-skip" data-ad-bar="1" data-aspect-ratio="0.5625" data-blurb="true" data-org="wapo" data-playthrough="true" data-uuid="9eaa12a4-e673-4678-95c3-c213c34a3c65"></div></div></figure></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">An <a href="http://maristpoll.marist.edu/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/NPR_PBS-NewsHour_Marist-Poll_USA-NOS-and-Tables_1909261000.pdf#page=3">NPR-PBS NewsHour-Marist poll</a> conducted Wednesday found that 49 percent of Americans supported opening an impeachment inquiry while 46 percent were opposed. And in a <a href="https://www.huffpost.com/entry/impeachment-ukraine-trump-poll_n_5d8d0f12e4b0019647a5811f?guccounter=1">Huffington Post-YouGov poll</a> completed Thursday, 47 percent said that Trump should be impeached and removed from office, up slightly from 43 percent earlier this month. The increase was driven more by increased support among Democrats than among independents.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Polls taken earlier in the week, before details of the Ukraine call were known, showed somewhat less support for impeachment. In a <a href="https://poll.qu.edu/national/release-detail?ReleaseID=3641">Quinnipiac University survey</a> completed on Monday, 37 percent of registered voters supported impeaching and removing the president; 57 percent were opposed, including nearly all Republicans, 58 percent of independents, and 21 percent of Democrats.</p></div><div><div></div></div><div><h3 class="font--subhead color-gray-darkest ma-0">A lose-lose</h3></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Rosa Kee cant stand Trump, but for a long time, she thought impeachment was the wrong idea: I really wanted us to <span>vote</span> him out, because otherwise hed say, This isnt what the people wanted.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_4"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_4"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">But this week, Kee, a former telecom employee from Stone Mountain, Ga., changed her mind. Kee is now, grudgingly, okay with the Democrats pressing toward impeachment.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">This feels different to me, said Kee, 73. Back when he said to Putin, Russia, if youre listening, go after Hillary, I thought, Okay, thats just his ego talking. But what he did to this Ukrainian guy, now hes using his position for his own interests.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Kee still doesnt like the idea of Congress removing Trump  a decision she thinks voters should make on their own  but she believes House Democrats are making a principled decision, even if shes certain it wont succeed.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">It will help the Democrats because they finally did something about him, she said. But I fear it will help Trump, too, because hes always making himself out to be the victim, and that always works for him.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_5"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_5"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Impeachment  Congresss power to remove a president without a vote by the people  has never been popular. In the 1970s with Republican Richard Nixon and in the 1990s with Democrat Bill Clinton, a majority of Americans concluded that the president had behaved badly. But the country remained largely opposed to impeachment until shortly before Nixon resigned, and in Clintons case, all the way through his acquittal by the Senate.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In Washington, the Ukraine story sucked the air out of every other issue. In Iowa and other early primary states, Democratic presidential candidates watched as news coverage pivoted from the campaign to impeachment. Political consultants and pundits shifted into hyper-speculation mode, urgently searching for clues about how the impeachment probe might alter the countrys political path.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In swing districts, the Ukraine call and impeachment inquiry didnt seem quite the watershed events they were in the capital, but some voters welcomed the move.</p></div><div><div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In the Yorba Linda, Calif., townhouse development where Frank Bryant lives, some neighbors no longer speak to each other because of their opposing views on Trump. Its way too personal, so nobody talks politics anymore around the community pool, said Bryant, a professor of marketing at nearby Cal Poly Pomona.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_6"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_6"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">He generally votes for Democrats, but he admires how Trump has managed the economy. Now, Bryants ready to go along with House Speaker Nancy Pelosis decision to switch gears and embrace impeachment.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">I think we have to go with the speaker right now, Bryant said. Shes been very careful, and so, if she sees something there now, I believe her.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Voters on both sides echoed Pelosis concerns earlier this year that an impeachment drive could hurt Democrats. Trump supporters and opponents alike predicted that the move might strengthen Trumps reelection bid.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The modern history of impeachment demonstrates that a sitting president can indeed turn the tables on his accusers, said Frank O. Bowman III, a professor at the University of Missouri School of Law and author of <a href="https://www.cambridge.org/core/books/high-crimes-and-misdemeanors/06FDD57E104F3891A4C2B50175195FA5">High Crimes and Misdemeanors</a>, a history of impeachment. Bowman said that Clinton effectively pressed his case in the news media, portraying his Republican opponents as bad guys who wanted to use his extramarital sexual affair to remove him from office.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_7"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_7"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Clinton managed to flip the public narrative from his own bad behavior to the behavior of those who attacked him, the historian said. Trump doesnt need Clinton to teach him anything about fighting dirty. Any attempt to impeach Trump is going to invite the nastiest kinds of backlash, first of all against Joe Biden.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In St. Clair Shores, a sharply split district in Detroits northern suburbs, Diana Rascano, 69, said she often votes for Democrats in local elections, where government touches your life more than the feds. But in presidential votes, shes a consistent Republican because of her conservative views on abortion, immigration and taxes.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The transcript of the presidents call with his Ukrainian counterpart sounded like standard business talk to her, not unlike what she recalls from her days as an executive at the Detroit Edison utility company.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Rascano said Democrats, some Republicans and the news media are acting as one big angry mob in ... a constant barrage of trying to find a crime committed by Trump. As a result, she said, shes more supportive of the president in 2020 than she was in 2016.</p></div><div><div></div></div><div><h3 class="font--subhead color-gray-darkest ma-0">Switching sides</h3></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In northwestern Pennsylvania, Trump in 2016 became the first Republican presidential candidate to carry Erie County in more than three decades. White working-class voters abandoned their historical ties to the Democratic Party after manufacturing plants downsized or closed along Lake Eries southern shore.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_8"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_8"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">But last year, county voters shifted their loyalties back to Democrats as Gov. Tom Wolf and Sen. Robert P. Casey Jr. both carried the county by about 20 points.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In Harborcreek, a working-class town just east of Erie city, many residents said they werent paying much attention to the unfolding impeachment controversy in Washington.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Jim Cass, a 77-year-old retired bar owner who has been a Republican all his life, has never liked Trump and said the Ukraine matter has only validated his view.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">I think he is a liar and a cheat and I never trusted him with our foreign affairs, Cass said, and I dont like anything about him. Period.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Hes all for impeaching the president, but he isnt sure Congress will be able to amass sufficient evidence to get the job done, and he worries that the debate will deepen the nations divisions.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Hes certain the debate will exacerbate divisions within his own family. He has a son and a son-in-law who loves Trump, but another son and a daughter-in-law who dont have any use for him, either.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">But Cass said the risk of more family fights is worth it if the result is removing from office the man he considers mentally ill.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">To another Republican in Harborcreek, though, the move toward impeachment seems a recipe for a Trump victory in 2020. Randy Wienke, a 64-year-old truck driver, has been stuck in the house for several days recovering from back surgery  plenty of time to absorb details of the Ukraine story on Fox News.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Hes concluded that Democrats are just out to remove Trump over a phone call that he said most voters dont care about. They just dont like him, and they dont like him because he doesnt play into their little clique politics game there, Wienke said.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Hes convinced that the real criminals are Joe Biden and his son Hunter, who have been the target of Trumps counterattack this week.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Even if Trump did do something wrong, Wienke said, he doesnt understand why Democrats would rush to push him from office: Who would take his place? Mike Pence? They still would not be getting rid of any of his conservative, Republican political views.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The impeachment initiative has changed some minds  if not about Trump, then about the Democrats lining up against him.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Tom Shaw, 56, a fraud investigator in Henrico, Va., voted for Democrat Barack Obama in 2008, Republican Mitt Romney in 2012 and then Trump in the last election, in good part because he liked the idea of a businessperson managing the country.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Business is tough and running this country is like a big business, Shaw said. Hes been pleased to see Trump cut red tape, lower unemployment, reduce corporate tax rates and sign a criminal justice reform bill.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">But Shaw switched gears last year to vote against his Republican congressman, Dave Brat, and choose Democrat Abigail Spanberger because shed served as a CIA officer and promised to work with Republicans.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">He wont vote for her again, though, because of her strong advocacy for gun control  and because she announced her support for impeachment this week.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Id love to see her sit down and lay out the specific facts that are illegal involving Trump, he said. But well see. Maybe something comes out in the hearings. If theres evidence that Trump violated some law or did something unethical, I would vote to impeach him in a second.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Portnoy reported from Chesterfield, Va.; Wilson from Yorba Linda, Calif.; Craig from Erie, Pa.; and Fisher from Washington. Anna Clark in Detroit; Jared Leone in Dunedin, Fla.; Eva Ruth Moravec in Georgetown, Tex.; and Scott Clement contributed to this report.</p></div></section></div></div><div class="mb-lg pad-bottom-xs
